  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_148f9464-8292-4cc1-81b1-f4332583390d'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14373753935017783193">Lucinda Barrett's best friends ended up married to the men to whom they delivered their "lessons in love." So Lucinda decides to choose someone who definitely needs lessons, but someone who will not complicate her life. And that person is definitely not Robert Carroway.<br/><br/>Robert is nothing if not complicated, and though he is the brother of a viscount, he rarely goes about so</span>
  <span id="freeText14373753935017783193" style="display:none">Lucinda Barrett's best friends ended up married to the men to whom they delivered their "lessons in love." So Lucinda decides to choose someone who definitely needs lessons, but someone who will not complicate her life. And that person is definitely not Robert Carroway.<br /><br />Robert is nothing if not complicated, and though he is the brother of a viscount, he rarely goes about society, and finds the weather and hat fashions ludicrous subjects for discussion. Robert is attracted to Lucinda's unpretentious ways, her serenity and her kindness. When she chooses someone for her love lessons, Robert offers to help her deliver her lessons, but sets out to convince the woman he has fallen for to take a chance on love... and on him.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_31392983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31392983" />
    <a title="Eastofoz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz"><img alt="Eastofoz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203907098p2/939365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31392983?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eastofoz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eastofoz" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz">Eastofoz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers looking for a severely emotionally scarred hero</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=historical-regency">historical-regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31392983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17677712636700689468">I was a bit leery about this story so it took me a while to finally decide to read it because the hero is a reclusive, severely emotionally scarred man due to the war. Robert pops up in the previous book “London’s Perfect Scoundrel” as a war hero who barely says two words to anyone and just doesn’t seem all that interesting. He’s impossible to categorize too as an alpha, beta or gamma hero which was interesting to see. Basically I had a hard time seeing how he could be hero material. Well he tur</span>
  <span id="freeText17677712636700689468" style="display:none">I was a bit leery about this story so it took me a while to finally decide to read it because the hero is a reclusive, severely emotionally scarred man due to the war. Robert pops up in the previous book “London’s Perfect Scoundrel” as a war hero who barely says two words to anyone and just doesn’t seem all that interesting. He’s impossible to categorize too as an alpha, beta or gamma hero which was interesting to see. Basically I had a hard time seeing how he could be hero material. Well he turns out to be not only an incredible hero, but a man with a beautiful soul. He has such emotional strength when all is said and done that you can’t help but adore him.<br /><br />There’s no squabbling or love/hate or any of the standard lines you often find in historicals to make the characters interesting. This one was very different with an unlikely man slowly coming into his own with the help of Lucinda Barrett. The demons he fights just to stay sane really give you the shivers. You can feel the battle he wages on a constant basis when these panic attacks hit him, but he wants to help Lucinda because it somehow helps him leave his solitary world and make it through the day. That might sound hokey and typical but I didn’t think it was at all. His strength of character is amazing especially in the face of hellish odds as you see his story unravel. The two start off as acquaintances, turn into friends and then friends “with benefits” ;-)<br /><br />Enoch is a master at dialog. She’s excellent at showing interruptions in conversation so that you feel like you’re right there listening to the characters speaking. This is the kind of book that moves along so smoothly you’re surprised that it’s already over. The sexual tension between the “friends” is very high throughout the book and though it could’ve used a smidge more ‘bedroom scenes’ (what is there is very good though) the emotional side made up for it –which is saying a lot about how good a writer she is. There are some very sad moments as well as very funny ones. The parallel drawn between Robert’s growing roses and how they bloom is very good. Something that could’ve turned out to be cheesy or predictable was actually a nice touch to the whole story adding even more feeling. At the start of each chapter there are also a few lines from Mary Shelley's <i>Frankenstein</i>. This sets the tone for the chapter so the reader knows if they should anticipate something good or bad as well as getting further insight into Robert who feels like he's a wretched outcast just as Frankenstein's monster felt --very well-done.<br /><br />Previous characters from other books (the other ladies who taught their ‘lessons’, Tristan, Saint, the Duke of Wycliff) all make an appearance which was nice to see. If you like series’ books this adds a nice touch of familiarity making you feel like you ‘know’ something that others may not. You’ll find yourself smiling also from start to finish –it’s the kind of read that just makes you feel happy.<br /><br />The “Lessons in Love” series was fantastic and this final one was a fitting end to some smart women and their sexy, if flawed men. Keeper material :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17677712636700689468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652279556" />
    <a title="Addie H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16858463-addie-h"><img alt="Addie H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511793475p2/16858463.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/652279556?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addie H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addie H" href="/user/show/16858463-addie-h">Addie H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16858463-addie-h?shelf=zn-unrequited-love">zn-unrequited-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16858463-addie-h?shelf=zp-scar-physical">zp-scar-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16858463-addie-h?shelf=zz-cryfest">zz-cryfest</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652279556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8210244872443925674">I am re-reading all my 5 star rated romance novels. There are 60 on my shelf. This is book 19. <br/><br/><i>(Tropes: Unrequited Love, Tortured Hero (PTSD, limp)</i> <br/><br/>This is how my 19th re-read held up. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475178013ra/20692599.gif' width='350' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>*****<br/><i>For three years he'd looked forward to seeing Lucinda, even from a distance. Close to her, interacting with her, she felt like daylight after a very long, very dark night. He couldn't help stretching his wings a little, yet he still lingered in the shadows, afraid the sun would burn him to ashes. But he'd ma</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8210244872443925674" style="display:none">I am re-reading all my 5 star rated romance novels. There are 60 on my shelf. This is book 19. <br><br><i>(Tropes: Unrequited Love, Tortured Hero (PTSD, limp)</i> <br><br>This is how my 19th re-read held up. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475178013ra/20692599.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>*****<br><i>For three years he'd looked forward to seeing Lucinda, even from a distance. Close to her, interacting with her, she felt like daylight after a very long, very dark night. He couldn't help stretching his wings a little, yet he still lingered in the shadows, afraid the sun would burn him to ashes. But he'd made her a bargain, and she remained as alluring as candlelight to a moth.</i><br>*****<br><br>Quick plot: Lucianda Barret wants a husband who is aimable, one who will create no chaos in her orderly life, one who will help her take care of her father as he grows older. And she thinks she has found it in Lord Geoffrey. The why can’t she stop thinking about the wounded war hero, Robert “Bit” Carroway, brother of her best friend’s husband?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530214632ra/25879345.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Robert is one of those characters, like Ian from The Madness of Lord Ian McKenzie, you just want to heal with the power of hugs and love. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492872226ra/22562826.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although it probably would not do Robert’s PTSD any good. Because Robert is one wounded hero. <br><br>- Sweet Lucifer. What had he been thinking? That he could go back to who he used to be, that he could dance and laugh and find a woman attractive as if nothing had ever happened? <br>He had no right to any of it. <br>For God's sake, he was supposed to be dead. And the dead knew nothing but darkness.<br>He hunched down in the corner, rocking back and forth.<br>Stop it, stop it, stop it.<br><br>But unlike everyone else who tiptoes around him, Lucinda treats Robert normally. She sees the need in him to have something positive to focus on. So she teaches him about her hobby of tending roses. <br><br>- Flowers, plants, growing things. Things that didn't scream or bleed when they died. Things that wouldn't look at you oddly if you didn't know what the hell you were doing. By God, it actually made sense. <br><br>In exchange, he says he will help her snare the husband she thinks she wants. Despite really wanting her to himself. <br><br>- If he'd been himself, the Robert before the war, he would have thought Georgiana was matchmaking. Back then he would have pursued Lucinda, though in truth it would have been her looks that attracted him. Now she'd set her sights on someone else. And now it was her serenity, her peace, that drew him like a warm breeze on a cold day. And even though he enjoyed being around her, he resisted her, because he was supremely aware that he wasn't the old Robert any longer; he was Bit, a piece of what he'd once been.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530214632ra/25879346.gif" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While in Robert’s company, Lucinda keeps finding herself utterly drawn to his frankness. <br><br>- "I… got out of the habit of it, I think, and now I spend so much time thinking about it that the chance to speak sometimes passes me by."<br> "You talk to me."<br> "You're easy to talk to."<br> Her cheeks warmed.<br><br>And the rest as they say….<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530214632ra/25879347.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- Before he could convince himself of the idiocy of his impulse or think where their chaperone might be, he leaned over and touched his mouth to hers. For a second, for a heartbeat, time stopped. And then he made himself straighten, before she could pull away. <br><br>- "You didn't mean to kiss me," she interrupted, backing away and nearly tripping over his borrowed cane. "That's all right."<br> "No, I didn't mean to upset you," he countered, limping forward to retrieve the cane from the tangle of her skirts. "I meant to kiss you."<br> "Oh. Why?" she asked, still stammering and uncomfortably hot beneath her thin muslin gown.<br> "If I told you that, I don't think we would be able to remain friends," he said, his gaze still on her mouth. "And we are still friends, aren't we?"<br><br>- "You don't need my nightmares, Lucinda. You talk to me like I'm human, and that's enough."<br> They passed between a tall stand of pink rhododendron and an empty coach stopped at the edge of the street, and abruptly she couldn't stand it any longer. <br>If she couldn't touch him, comfort him, do something, it would cause her physical pain. Tightening her grip on his arm, she pulled him around and leaned up to tangle her fingers through his hair, drew his face down, and kissed him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530214632ra/25879344.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- He waltzed well, she realized, easy and graceful and his limp barely noticeable. His knee would hurt tomorrow, probably, but she had to think that that was the least of his worries at the moment.<br>"I'm beginning to wish I was amiable," he murmured.<br>She swallowed, because she'd been thinking the same thing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530214632ra/25879343.gif" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***** <br><br>5 stars!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494368992ra/22708713.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_67484770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67484770" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67484770?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=regency-napoleonic-era">regency-napoleonic-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67484770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2027821992724018955"><i> When it’s Lucinda Barrett turn to give her lessons in love, she already has her eye on one gentleman, who will keep her life uneventful. Lucinda’s lessons are going without a hitch and uneventful until Robert Carroway walks in to help her give her lessons a helping hand, and Lucinda’s and Roberts’ lives becomes very complicated</i><br/><br/><br/> The last of the The Lessons of Love Trilogy, this series was wonderful and ending on a very high note with England's Perfect Hero!<br/> Out of the three friends Lucinda is th</span>
  <span id="freeText2027821992724018955" style="display:none"><i> When it’s Lucinda Barrett turn to give her lessons in love, she already has her eye on one gentleman, who will keep her life uneventful. Lucinda’s lessons are going without a hitch and uneventful until Robert Carroway walks in to help her give her lessons a helping hand, and Lucinda’s and Roberts’ lives becomes very complicated</i><br /><br /><br /> The last of the The Lessons of Love Trilogy, this series was wonderful and ending on a very high note with England's Perfect Hero!<br /> Out of the three friends Lucinda is the straightlaced no nonsense thinking lady, when it’s her turn to give her lessons she chooses a man whom won’t complicate her life, someone whom would know taking care of her father the General. Lucinda’s lessons are going okay, until she runs into Robert Carroway, who offers his help to help her with her student as a trade for the roses she gave him. But when her thoughts turn to Robert then her student, and when she must clear Robert’s name, Lucinda’s in for her own lessons in love.<br /><br /> Robert Carroway, was capture and tortured for seven months, and was almost killed, due to the tragic events, Robert has been in a state of being alive then living. Suffering from dark panic attacks, when a chance face to face encounter with Lucinda gives him the first step out his darkness, Robert offers to help Lucinda, but at the same time, sees a chance to get closer to her, but with his misgivings of being able to give her a normal life with him, Robert holds back, until events leads them to being tied together forever..in love...<br /><br /> I loved both Lucinda and Robert but I was mostly looking forward to Robert or Bit’s story the most. Robert was the torture hero, whom lived day to day but wasn’t living until Lucinda walked into his life. With Lucinda, she was a fresh breeze to him, and as he helped her with her lessons, he was also getting a lesson on living, and giving Lucinda a lesson of her own to not just settle for less and easy. Robert clawed his way back from the dead, and knew Lucinda deserved more then to just settle. He showed Lucinda what it meant to go for more, but at the same time Lucinda taught Robert to be at peace with himself again. Robert was just amazing, as he waltzed with the wallflowers, proved to Lucinda’s father he wasn’t a traitor and learned to love and live again. <br /> Lucinda was raised by her father a great war General, she always puts others needs first, but always settled for less herself. Robert shows her a hard lot in life from his past, but shows her to go for the goal for herself and trust in love. Lucinda was kind and loved Robert and trusted him, when she knew her father couldn’t be counted on. This showed how she believed in Robert and his good heart.<br /><br /> Robert’s family was as always very supported of Robert, it was funny the way each took care and helped Robert from Tristan dumping cold water on him to break him out of panic attack, to Andrew dancing a waltz with him( Andrew even hummed a offkey tune!)<br /> In the beginning of each chapter, there was a little snippet of Frankenstein, which gives the reader an insight of the upcoming chapter but SE took liberty with the timeline of Frankenstein as she refers to Mary Shelley by name when the first edition was published anonymously in 1818 the book’s time setting MS wasn't named the author until 1823. (yeah, my inner historian kicked in *sighs*)<br /><br />overall: The ending to the Lesson in Love Trilogy, and the England's Perfect Hero ..ends on a perfectly high note!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2027821992724018955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1374377087" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374377087" />
    <a title="Jultri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11762474-jultri"><img alt="Jultri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514197791p2/11762474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374377087?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jultri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jultri" href="/user/show/11762474-jultri">Jultri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11762474-jultri?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11762474-jultri?shelf=keepers">keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11762474-jultri?shelf=maimed-hero">maimed-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374377087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13443259235723440463">4.5/5. Rounded up because the Carroway sibling love is the real deal. A reread and it held onto its original rating in 2013. Robert makes a most unique hero. A PTSD afflicted hero is nothing new but Enoch describes his anxiety so well and he differs from others in that he is not willing to let it consume him, to give in to the rage and the darkness. No, he tries to fight it all the way, even as the sudden onslaught of an attack threatens to suffocate and consume him, he clings on to some glimmer</span>
  <span id="freeText13443259235723440463" style="display:none">4.5/5. Rounded up because the Carroway sibling love is the real deal. A reread and it held onto its original rating in 2013. Robert makes a most unique hero. A PTSD afflicted hero is nothing new but Enoch describes his anxiety so well and he differs from others in that he is not willing to let it consume him, to give in to the rage and the darkness. No, he tries to fight it all the way, even as the sudden onslaught of an attack threatens to suffocate and consume him, he clings on to some glimmer of lightness - the budding of rose cuttings, his family's unconditional love, and the positivity and warmth of the luminous Lucinda Barrett. <br /><br />Lucinda had a noticeable presence on the periphery of his sphere even before Robert went to war. Three years after his return from the Napoleon War, an acclaimed war hero but still a ghost of the charming, extroverted man he used to be. His physical injuries still cause him pain and disability but it is the psychological scars that have maimed his soul. Now a silent recluse even within the bosom of his well-meaning and protective family, his crippling panic attacks hinder his attempt to claw back his old life, even as he will his family not to give up on him. <br /><br />Despite flailing in the dark, he does not allow himself to sink but grabs hold of a lifeline - Lucinda, a close family friend. He repeatedly and unexpectedly pops into her path and consciousness, simultaneously igniting her irritation and curiosity equally with a few chosen enigmatic words only to disappear as quietly as he arrived. They form a tentative partnership and friendship; in helping Lucinda with her project of training her chosen potential husband to be worthy of her, Robert finds a buoy to keep him afloat. He is a complex man with torturous, dark secrets -secrets that involve Lucinda's father, a highly respected general. Even as their friendship very slowly turns to deeper passion, there are such much in the way of a future together. His past, their present circumstances. <br /><br />*Sigh* Thank you to my fellow buddy readers, because this was such a satisfying read. I can't stress enough how wonderful Robert is as a character. None of that self-pitying, rage-against-the-world behaviour we have come to expect of returned soldiers in HRs. And his siblings are so magnificent in their subtle and not so subtle unquestionable support of him. Lucinda too is a great character, astute and just as cunning a strategist as her father. Yes, the concept of her lessons are silly, hence the 1/2 star deduction, but the quality and depth of the writing permits the reader to easily overlook this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13443259235723440463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

It’s a beautiful, touching romance between an emotionally and physically scarred hero suffering from PTSD and the woman whose friendship helps heal his wounded soul and bring him back into the light. I absol</span>
  <span id="freeText7910850633857474516" style="display:none">5+ stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br /><br />As much as I enjoyed the love/hate banter of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/823583.The_Rake__Lessons_in_Love___1_" title="The Rake (Lessons in Love, #1) by Suzanne Enoch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rake</a> and swooned at devilishly wicked, sinfully charming rake Saint’s feet in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1032696.London_s_Perfect_Scoundrel__Lessons_in_Love___2_" title="London's Perfect Scoundrel (Lessons in Love, #2) by Suzanne Enoch" rel="nofollow noopener">London's Perfect Scoundrel</a>, <b>England’s Perfect Hero</b> ended up being my favorite book in Enoch’s wonderful <i>Lessons in Love</i> trilogy. It’s a beautiful, touching romance between an emotionally and physically scarred hero suffering from PTSD and the woman whose friendship helps heal his wounded soul and bring him back into the light. I absolutely <i>loved</i> it! My only complaint is the same that I had about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1032696.London_s_Perfect_Scoundrel__Lessons_in_Love___2_" title="London's Perfect Scoundrel (Lessons in Love, #2) by Suzanne Enoch" rel="nofollow noopener">London's Perfect Scoundrel</a>, which is that it needed a bit more to the ending and an epilogue. But it’s still a heartrending, soulful love story worthy of big 5 stars! <br /> <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The scene where Robert dances with all the wallflowers at a ball, despite his difficulty with touch and at the detriment to his injured leg, because it’s important to Lucinda was sweet, sigh-worthy, and exceedingly romantic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_844589232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/844589232" />
    <a title="Vintage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27204643-vintage"><img alt="Vintage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475253836p2/27204643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/844589232?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vintage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vintage" href="/user/show/27204643-vintage">Vintage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=bromance-alert">bromance-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=virgin">virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=this-guys-in-love-with-you">this-guys-in-love-with-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=slow-burn">slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=read-and-reread">read-and-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=nicely-done">nicely-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=honor">honor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=bamboozled-hero">bamboozled-hero</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer844589232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12123436893893440470">A comfort re-read and very satisfying in these troubling times, so thank you Ms. Enoch.<br/><br/>Robert, the H, suffers from PTSD as a result of being tortured in a French prison for seven months. If that weren't bad enough no one knows what happened to him so it's easy for rumors to begin circulating that he was/is a potential traitor.<br/><br/>The heroine is caught between a rock and a hard place as she has her eyes on a more suitable hero, one that her ex-General father approves of and can easily ring his own be</span>
  <span id="freeText12123436893893440470" style="display:none">A comfort re-read and very satisfying in these troubling times, so thank you Ms. Enoch.<br /><br />Robert, the H, suffers from PTSD as a result of being tortured in a French prison for seven months. If that weren't bad enough no one knows what happened to him so it's easy for rumors to begin circulating that he was/is a potential traitor.<br /><br />The heroine is caught between a rock and a hard place as she has her eyes on a more suitable hero, one that her ex-General father approves of and can easily ring his own bell, but becomes attracted to the very unsuitable and uncommunicative hero.<br /><br />Best friends with his SIL, there is a very slow burn attraction between Robert and Lucinda as she wants to help him adapt to real life. After three years of being shut down, he is slowly ready to embrace life. The heroine helps him set up a rose garden for him to tend that serves as a nice metaphor for his reintroduction to life. Enoch could have done more with it.<br /><br />Enoch provides extra layers of story with the friendship between Lucinda and the other heroines in this series as well as the strong, supportive and loving relationship between the hero and his brothers. His relationship with his brothers is a big plus and the H has a lot of brothers.<br /><br />The weakest point is the McGuffin of the purloined letters that may drag England back into a war. This is a level of MI6/007 espionage Regency style that I don't feel is dealt with appropriately. Would it really have been that easy to steal something that could drag England back into war and what kind of papers could they be?<br /><br />Ah well, it doesn't really matter as we have an emergent hero befuddled with a heroine who leads him to the light.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12123436893893440470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=to-blog">to-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45258665&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer45258665" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7975141132119123382">I loved Robert, the tortured hero who suffered from PTSD, and I liked following his journey towards recovery - even though it wasn´t easy to "witness" his panic attacks.<br/><br/>I adored his family (his brothers - especially little Edward, the Runt - and his sister-in-law Georgie) and friends (Saint and Evie), who played more than secondary roles in the story. That was good, as it´s unusual to see secondary characters acting out like that.<br/><br/>At first, I liked Lucinda, the heroine, but she wasn´t nothing "ou</span>
  <span id="freeText7975141132119123382" style="display:none">I loved Robert, the tortured hero who suffered from PTSD, and I liked following his journey towards recovery - even though it wasn´t easy to "witness" his panic attacks.<br /><br />I adored his family (his brothers - especially little Edward, the Runt - and his sister-in-law Georgie) and friends (Saint and Evie), who played more than secondary roles in the story. That was good, as it´s unusual to see secondary characters acting out like that.<br /><br />At first, I liked Lucinda, the heroine, but she wasn´t nothing "out of this world". I mean, she was nice, sensible and kind, something like "the girl next door". Then, BAM!, she went and betrayed Robert´s confidence and, no matter how quickly this issue was resolved between them - thank you, Ms. Enoch, for not dragging us into a "Big Misunderstanding" plot device - and how she immediately redeemed herself, I couldn´t forget that.<br /><br />As for the story, I really liked it. It was kinda slow at first, but that was expected considering that Robert was still in the first stages of his recovery. The second half, when he had to fight for his innocence, was more action paced and I was almost biting my nails when Robert, his brother Tristan and his friend Wycliffe broke into Geoffrey´s house. BTW, it was pretty easy to figure out who the villain was, but that didn´t detract me from the story because I wasn´t reading this book for its mystery/suspense part.</span>

<div id="review_3373641983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373641983" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57282794-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505016022p2/57282794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3373641983?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/57282794-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=ex-military">ex-military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=napoleonic">napoleonic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3373641983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11786070885544643339">3.5 to 4 stars. I enjoyed this book about a very damaged hero who had been imprisoned and tortured by some of Napoleon's henchmen around the time of the Battle of Waterloo. He had barely made it out alive, with severe physical injuries, but with even deeper mental scars. His PTSD chiefly manifested itself as withdrawal from society, even from his family.<br/><br/>The heroine, Lucinda, becomes involved with him when he accidentally overhears her (somewhat childish) plans to teach another man some lessons a</span>
  <span id="freeText11786070885544643339" style="display:none">3.5 to 4 stars. I enjoyed this book about a very damaged hero who had been imprisoned and tortured by some of Napoleon's henchmen around the time of the Battle of Waterloo. He had barely made it out alive, with severe physical injuries, but with even deeper mental scars. His PTSD chiefly manifested itself as withdrawal from society, even from his family.<br /><br />The heroine, Lucinda, becomes involved with him when he accidentally overhears her (somewhat childish) plans to teach another man some lessons about the proper way to live one's life. Fortunately, this slightly silly aspect of the plot is soon left behind, as Robert, or 'Bit' as he is affectionately known by his family, gradually starts to come out of his shell, to find a way to the light, and begin to really live his life again.<br /><br />There is no doubting that Robert is the key character in this book. Lucinda is kind and loving, but she acts as a kind of foil for this charming, wonderful man who has been so deeply hurt. His family love him very deeply but don't know how to help him. It's lovely to see his resigned patience with their fumbling attempts to understand and help him. It's also lovely to see how he gradually begins to heal under the warm, understanding 'sun' of Lucinda's patient, understated and caring attention to him.<br /><br />The author writes Robert's slow and steady journey back to himself very well IMO. It was well-paced, and showed beautiful insight. It kept you reading. You SO wanted Robert to recover.<br /><br />There was a mystery storyline in this book, and (as usual for me) it took me a while to work out who the bad guy was. I did figure it out (for once) before the actual reveal though LOL. I have to admit, for me the book began to drag a little around the 3/4 mark. It seemed to be taking too long for the parameters of the mystery to be laid out. Cut to the chase already! This took off a half star for me. The last section of the book was quite enjoyable though, as Robert, aided by his delightful family and friends, chased down and caught the bad guy.<br /><br />I thought Ms Enoch wrote the secondary characters very well: Lucinda's father General Barrett with his military interests, the up-and-coming Geoffrey who had hopes of gaining a promotion to Major in India, and Bit's lovely brothers, including the youngest one who was a lively and interesting character all his own. We didn't see too much of Lucinda's female friends, but as I hadn't read the previous books that wasn't an issue for me. <br /><br />I did like the short quotes from 'Frankenstein' at the start of each chapter. They were quite apt, and IMO really added to the story, especially as Robert had been, understandably, a little obsessed with rereading the book.<br /><br />Overall, a sensitively written book showing excellent historical knowledge, and an insight into some of the challenges returned veterans would have faced. I enjoyed the romance aspect as well. I don't intend to read the first two books as they don't sound as good, but who knows? I may try another of this writer's books at some stage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11786070885544643339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49934022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15740953913127469757">Mayhap SE is just not my cuppa, 'cuz this book was simply ho-hum. The storyline was blah, the H/H & 2ndary characters weren't well-rounded. From the get-go, it's quite obvious who stole the papers from House Guards. Too much dialogue & too many characters were crammed in-between the covers, 'overcrowded' = the operative word here. Bit has been living w/ his sibling since his horrific captivity, so his clandestine meetings w/ Luce took place @ her home. When I think of a 'reclusive' hero, I visua</span>
  <span id="freeText15740953913127469757" style="display:none">Mayhap SE is just not my cuppa, 'cuz this book was simply ho-hum. The storyline was blah, the H/H &amp; 2ndary characters weren't well-rounded. From the get-go, it's quite obvious who stole the papers from House Guards. Too much dialogue &amp; too many characters were crammed in-between the covers, 'overcrowded' = the operative word here. Bit has been living w/ his sibling since his horrific captivity, so his clandestine meetings w/ Luce took place @ her home. When I think of a 'reclusive' hero, I visualize him living in his own domain =)~. He's quite helpless in his attempts to clear his name. Sexual tension = nada, @ least, none that I could discern. Luce was obtuse, putting 2 &amp; 2 together &amp; coming up w/ 3, w/ all the incriminating clues pointing @ her suitor as the culprit. I'd have liked her a li'l bit more if she'd put more faith in Robert &amp; less in her suitor, plus, she didn't want to help Bit out. She chose to be neutral &amp; it was way too late - for me - when she finally changed her tune. The whole book was a major exercise for Bit to 'live' again, thru' the process of falling for Luce &amp; growing roses, w/ the lame intrigue mixed in the pot. The abrupt ending was unsatisfactory.</span>

<div id="review_2566380769" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566380769" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3919132-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507125560p2/3919132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566380769?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/3919132-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Linda by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3935451-ririn-aziz">Ririn Aziz</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=what-are-friends-for">what-are-friends-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=hero-was-a-soldier">hero-was-a-soldier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=ptsd">ptsd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=regency-romance">regency-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566380769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer475637346930455582">According to Goodreads, Suzanne Enoch wrote eleven series and ‘Lessons In Love’ was her most popular. I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833923.England_s_Perfect_Hero__Lessons_in_Love___3_' title='England's Perfect Hero (Lessons in Love, #3) by Suzanne Enoch' rel='nofollow noopener'>England's Perfect Hero</a>, the 3rd story, as a standalone. I enjoyed the followup with the characters from the first two stories. But, ‘You just said you didn’t read the first two books!?’ That is correct but I found the easy introduction of best friends with their now-husbands and family members a fun romp. Because of Ms. Enoch’s style of writing, I glided into the storyline. <br/><br/>Miss Lucinda B</span>
  <span id="freeText475637346930455582" style="display:none">According to Goodreads, Suzanne Enoch wrote eleven series and ‘Lessons In Love’ was her most popular. I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833923.England_s_Perfect_Hero__Lessons_in_Love___3_" title="England's Perfect Hero (Lessons in Love, #3) by Suzanne Enoch" rel="nofollow noopener">England's Perfect Hero</a>, the 3rd story, as a standalone. I enjoyed the followup with the characters from the first two stories. But, ‘You just said you didn’t read the first two books!?’ That is correct but I found the easy introduction of best friends with their now-husbands and family members a fun romp. Because of Ms. Enoch’s style of writing, I glided into the storyline. <br /><br />Miss Lucinda Barrett was the last of three friends to teach a man his ‘lessons’ and marry. She decided to take on a soldier and gentleman her father -a military man- favored. Little did she know that Robert Carroway, the younger brother of Tristan Carroway -Lord Dare- from the first story, was fascinated with her. While discreetly pursuing Geoffrey Newcombe, Robert was following Lucinda. It sounds crazy but the romance was pretty good. <br /><br />Robert was a former soldier with a big secret. He had PTSD and I appreciated Ms. Enoch not sugar-coating this awful disorder. My quibble was with Lucinda. She was a ‘good’ daughter and, because of that, she obeyed the general even though she knew what he asked of her was wrong. <br /><br />I see from all my GR friends that the jury is still out with this story. Some loved it and others gave it one or two stars and they all have valid reasons. I refer to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833923.England_s_Perfect_Hero__Lessons_in_Love___3_" title="England's Perfect Hero (Lessons in Love, #3) by Suzanne Enoch" rel="nofollow noopener">England's Perfect Hero</a> as a modern historical romance. When I read something of this nature, I expect the author to take liberties with the era. As for myself, I was won over because of the hero and his brothers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="475637346930455582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6649525-england-s-perfect-hero">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507262648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer740869462254982377">This was an interesting read for me. I don't usually like a book if I cannot feel the chemistry between the characters, which is true about this book, but I read it to the last line and followed its rather developed plots to the end, which is also a new experience with an Enoch book. <br/><br/>I was happy to find out that the hero for the 3rd book would be Robert, Tristan's war-injured brother. I literally went "yay" to my kindle. I thought him an interesting character in Tristan's story. Same thing goes </span>
  <span id="freeText740869462254982377" style="display:none">This was an interesting read for me. I don't usually like a book if I cannot feel the chemistry between the characters, which is true about this book, but I read it to the last line and followed its rather developed plots to the end, which is also a new experience with an Enoch book. <br /><br />I was happy to find out that the hero for the 3rd book would be Robert, Tristan's war-injured brother. I literally went "yay" to my kindle. I thought him an interesting character in Tristan's story. Same thing goes for Lucinda. I liked how level-headed and kind and considerate she is (unlike Georgiana who would be usually too headstrong and impulsive for me and Evie who is kind of boring). <br /><br />But lord do they make a boring couple. I kept turning the page waiting for the chemistry to happen. But it didn't happen for me in this book. For the life of me I just couldn't feel the attraction between them. Their interactions were missing something for me, I do not know what. Maybe it is Robert. I don't do well with a male leading character who is somehow a patient and the woman is his savior who saved him from his near-mental/near-death state. (This is usually the time I cue <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/360259.Flowers_from_the_Storm" title="Flowers from the Storm by Laura Kinsale" rel="nofollow noopener"> Flowers from the Storm</a>.) And Lucinda telling her father what Robert asked her not to tell another soul, I thought that was very uncool. I can understand why she did it, being close to her father and having faith in him and all, it was not that far-fetched an idea for her to do it. But it did not help with her character. <br /><br />But kudos to Enoch: I followed the story to the end because I just wanted to read on. She made me want to find out what happened in the story even though I was disappointed in the romance. In the end I read it like a myestery/war story. The romance was barely there. I never felt that Robert and Lucinda had feelings for each other, I was bored reading the 2 sex scenes, the stable one shocking. I also noticed that Enoch's heroines don't seem to know propriety. They are often virgins who have absolutely no problems losing their virginity to men who are at that time unlikely to pop the question. Not that I think you need the question to have sex, but do these women never think about the future? I find that a little hard to believe. They all give in a little too easily. I do not question the decision, but I question the ease with which they made the decision. <br /><br />The entire series appears to be one of Enoch's most popular series. I have consistently given all of them 3 stars. I don't know what to think of that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="740869462254982377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122690149" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18034325183943951398">This is the fourth Suzanne Enoch book I've read and the first one that I thought was very high quality. I really loved this.<br/><br/>Robert is a man suffering from ptsd in a time when no one knew what was going on from you. Returned home a POW he was beaten and whipped for speaking. Outside his family society has very little sympathy for a man that suffers from panic attacks from physical contact or even conversations.<br/><br/>Lucinda is practically engaged to a man mainly attracted to her because her father is a</span>
  <span id="freeText18034325183943951398" style="display:none">This is the fourth Suzanne Enoch book I've read and the first one that I thought was very high quality. I really loved this.<br /><br />Robert is a man suffering from ptsd in a time when no one knew what was going on from you. Returned home a POW he was beaten and whipped for speaking. Outside his family society has very little sympathy for a man that suffers from panic attacks from physical contact or even conversations.<br /><br />Lucinda is practically engaged to a man mainly attracted to her because her father is a general and it will further his career. She has a calming, non threatening way about her and I love the story arc of Robert opening up to her slowly. I also appreciated the courage Lucinda shows in defending Robert to other people.<br /><br />Suzanne Enoch did a good job of portraying a hurt hero without making him weak in the slightest, which isn't easy. I recommend this to anyone who is a fan of historical romances with tortured heroes.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_275883514" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275883514" />
    <a title="Huma Rashid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2845065-huma-rashid"><img alt="Huma Rashid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328728059p2/2845065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275883514?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Huma Rashid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Huma Rashid" href="/user/show/2845065-huma-rashid">Huma Rashid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2845065-huma-rashid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2845065-huma-rashid?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275883514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer308325193484148616">While I've been studying for the Bar, I found myself moving away from all the super-serious nonfiction books I've been reading for the past year (books about politics and history and prison and the like), and toward fun romances. I'm no longer puzzled at my shift in interest; I think it's quite expected that I'd want something really fun and light to read after spending all day hammering subjects like wills and torts and constitutional law. I need the escapism, and the books I've been reading la</span>
  <span id="freeText308325193484148616" style="display:none">While I've been studying for the Bar, I found myself moving away from all the super-serious nonfiction books I've been reading for the past year (books about politics and history and prison and the like), and toward fun romances. I'm no longer puzzled at my shift in interest; I think it's quite expected that I'd want something really fun and light to read after spending all day hammering subjects like wills and torts and constitutional law. I need the escapism, and the books I've been reading lately have delivered.<br /><br />EPH is the third in Suzanne Enoch's Lessons in Love trilogy (I haven't yet read the first one, but I've read the second!), and it's just delightful. I enjoyed all of it. A nice, slow build based on friendship, tons of intrigue built around the Napoleonic wars, a lovely family built around the hero and heroine (the hero's actual biological relatives, and the heroine's closest friends), a sensible and charming heroine, and a very damaged and intriguing hero. Those are all the ingredients necessary for me to just adore a romance novel.<br /><br />The male protagonist was probably my favorite aspect of this book. Not just a favorite character - a favorite *aspect,* because he informed so much of the novel, with his history in the war, and his relationship with the Carroway family. The entire book was built around him, but not in such a way that it felt like the female protagonist was being ignored. It was actually quite artfully done, and I love how Enoch structured it all. Aside from being a war hero, Robert Carroway suffered from severe PTSD. He had many war injuries (from being tortured - scars, basically), and a bad knee that caused him to limp slightly (but, of course, not TOO badly, not enough to sacrifice the romance novel staple of a capable, active hero). He suffered panic attacks. For a year after his return from France, he didn't speak a word to anyone. He cannot talk to people in polite society for more than a few minutes, if at all. He cannot stand being touched. He finds himself unable to understand or display the polite manners demanded by London society. He was, all in all, a great character, and he felt like the center of this novel in so many ways.<br /><br />This was an absolutely delightful and enjoyable story. I liked the second book in this series quite well, but this was even better. I suppose now I have to find the first book in this series, and read it. Coincidentally, it stars Robert's older brother Tristan, and his now-sister-in-law (and the female protagonist's BFF) Georgianna. It should be quite fun. <br /><br />Ah, thank you, Enoch, for making it just a little easier to deal with Bar stress. I don't like to whine about it (I know, I'm totally whining about it), and losing myself in a romance novel for a little over three hours is just the ticket to unwind. <br /><br />Reread August 2013.<br />Reread March 2016.</span>
  <a data-text-id="308325193484148616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061741715" href="/book/show/10179673-england-s-perfect-hero">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179743015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9569338030258947666">You guys, this was an amazing and delicious book. The hero and heroine were both such amazing endearing characters, I'm still reeling a bit.<br/><br/>Robert Carroway is a war hero who is suffering from a very severe case of PTSD. He's been almost a mute and a recluse for about 3 years, when he finally starts recovering enough to take baby steps back into Society. Lucinda is his sister-in-laws best friend, and when they have a discussion about her Lessons in Love plan, he sees her as a beacon of hope and h</span>
  <span id="freeText9569338030258947666" style="display:none">You guys, this was an amazing and delicious book. The hero and heroine were both such amazing endearing characters, I'm still reeling a bit.<br /><br />Robert Carroway is a war hero who is suffering from a very severe case of PTSD. He's been almost a mute and a recluse for about 3 years, when he finally starts recovering enough to take baby steps back into Society. Lucinda is his sister-in-laws best friend, and when they have a discussion about her Lessons in Love plan, he sees her as a beacon of hope and helping her with her plan is a way to come back to the living.<br /><br />What follows is a beautiful tale of what it takes Robert to come back to the living, and how their friendship evolves in so much more. Roberts PTSD is truly heartbreaking, and I loved how the whole recovery process was filled with set-backs and panic attacks. No magic healing trough the power of luuuuuurve, but simply getting better enough to love and live again. It was truly beautiful.<br /><br />By the end the whole recovery theme had to play second violin to a thievery and betrayal plot. Not that this part was badly written or even out of place, but the Roberts recovery was so beautiful to read, everything else is a bit pale compared with it. Still, both Robert and Lucinda as the great cast of side-characters shone in it, so I'm not complaining.<br /><br />I'm kinda angry with myself for jumping to the third installment of the series (the plots of the first two seemed so typical), but now that I've come to know the characters involved in those books, I'm definitely going to read those as well. But I had no troubles following this as a standalone, so I recommend it both on its own an as the bang ending to a series.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9569338030258947666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This is not a silly story - it's quite sad in some places - and I loved every page of it. <div id="review_3595745934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3595745934" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36459924-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589091840p2/36459924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3595745934?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/36459924-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36459924-irene?shelf=regency-romances-and-bodice-rippers">regency-romances-and-bodice-rippers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3595745934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9934322857110366457">When I read England's Perfect Hero when it first came out, I remember being disappointed.<br/><br/>Rereading this now, it doesn't compete because England's Perfect Hero is a complete 180 to London's Perfect Scoundrel, the previous book published in the Lessons in Love series. England's Perfect Hero, if you couldn't tell from the title, was an incredibly sweet and poignant story, and it was still sensual! Bit, a British captain tortured by the French, was an amazing hero. He was so sweet, when he was carin</span>
  <span id="freeText9934322857110366457" style="display:none">When I read England's Perfect Hero when it first came out, I remember being disappointed.<br /><br />Rereading this now, it doesn't compete because England's Perfect Hero is a complete 180 to London's Perfect Scoundrel, the previous book published in the Lessons in Love series. England's Perfect Hero, if you couldn't tell from the title, was an incredibly sweet and poignant story, and it was still sensual! Bit, a British captain tortured by the French, was an amazing hero. He was so sweet, when he was caring for his roses, when he danced with the wallflower at the ball, he is a great hero. <br /><br />Enoch nailed the POV for Lucinda AND Bit. Both of the characters worked because they were responding to each other. I lived for the simmering moments of sensuality and attraction. Whether it was Lucinda reminiscing about Bit as a dashing and attractive man before the war, and if he remembered they danced a quadrille in the past, or that one time Bit grinned and it took Lucinda's breath away. Sighh. <br /><br />There is this baseline of respect, care, and attention that both Lucinda and Bit have for each other. Their energy reminded me a lot of Brenda Joyce's The Stolen Bride. As much as Lucinda notices Bit, so too Bit notices Lucinda. When Bit tells Lucinda why she shouldn't be with Geoffrey - YOU ARE SETTLING, GIRL! - it was a wonderful moment. He wasn't trying to convince her he was the better man for her so much as he was telling her she deserved so much more than a lifeless marriage. <br /><br />I really enjoyed England's Perfect Hero. The ending was so sweet - it put a smile on my face and put a bow on the whole series. <br /><br />Also - HOW CUTE ARE SAINT AND EVIE!! They stole every scene they were in. <br /><br /><b>Lessons in Love ranking: </b><br /><b>1. London's Perfect Scoundrel </b>- this is one of Enoch's finest works. No one can compare to Saint and no one can compare to Saint and Evie together.<br /><b>2. England's Perfect Hero </b> - Bit and Lucinda are sweet to each other. If you enjoy tortured soldiers who don't believe they deserve love and perfect but still somehow relatable society girls, read this. And then read Brenda Joyce's The Stolen Bride. <br /><b>3. The Rake</b> - this is such a hot mess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9934322857110366457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2136313951" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136313951" />
    <a title="Rachmi " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3047938-rachmi"><img alt="Rachmi " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358842498p2/3047938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136313951?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachmi " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachmi " href="/user/show/3047938-rachmi">Rachmi </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=mental-illness-issue-disability">mental-illness-issue-disability</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136313951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8179460358941363245">If I should rate this book solely based on the relationship between the hero and heroine, Robert and Lucinda, I might give it more than 3 stars. There's a time I consider it a 4 stars worthy, as I think their story is the best in the trilogy. It's interesting and I loved it. I also liked the fact that Robert is so tortured with his past he isn't a rake or scoundrel like the previous heroes. <br/><br/>His PTSD is also pretty prominent it isn't hard to get the idea that he is really affected by the war. And</span>
  <span id="freeText8179460358941363245" style="display:none">If I should rate this book solely based on the relationship between the hero and heroine, Robert and Lucinda, I might give it more than 3 stars. There's a time I consider it a 4 stars worthy, as I think their story is the best in the trilogy. It's interesting and I loved it. I also liked the fact that Robert is so tortured with his past he isn't a rake or scoundrel like the previous heroes. <br /><br />His PTSD is also pretty prominent it isn't hard to get the idea that he is really affected by the war. And it makes Lucinda's present more makes sense to the development in his life. In a way I think their relationship is more understandable and real if I compare with the couple from the first two books. <br /><br />However, his PTSD also that makes me decided that it's a 3 stars reading for me, instead of a four. I get that he thinks that Lucinda is like his light to his darkness. She is his light, she makes his life better. And when he slowly but surely changing, his PTSD is suddenly disappeared. He doesn't mention it anymore and doesn't have any single episode after he confessed to himself that she makes him better.<br /><br />Now I believe that love and the right partner can make you become a better human being, but I don't think they can make your illness suddenly disappeared. As much as it is a good thing to happen, I don't buy it even a bit. <br /><br />I also cannot ignore how easy to guess who the bad guy is. Maybe it didn't mean to be unpredictable but the fact that the bad guy will justify Robert and Lucinda's relationship even more feels like a good set-up from the author. I prefer their relationship is free from the feeling that it's all arranged by the author. It isn't that big of a deal though. But I have to admit that I was quite frustrated with the way the characters trying to guess the bad guy while it's so clear to me.<br /><br />All in all, it is a nice ending for the trilogy. And it isn't a bad trilogy either, especially consider it's my first experience with Enoch books. However I won't right away try to get her other books, as the three were all only okay reading for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8179460358941363245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3442298749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer157667375979057574">I am beyond pleased that Robert Carroway is the hero in this book. I liked what I saw of Robert in the previous 2 of the series. <br/><br/>I didn't like some of the dynamic between the hero and heroine at times. Like after being physical together the first time, it was treated as a very underwhelming experience by the both of them. Meh.<br/><br/>Exciting conclusion. <br/><br/>3.5 stars.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WOHe5iOkyfSZDImguCEUWMTs36g6AZcVxgrQsi1XMAnjLzV4tuNrD3BMVvlXBENYofRAeT52gM2uDJTYNX/VTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WTqKdmmGHYLEM/pwgmQ+onKFFVWaXEIBsDvQFDoCEALi9GHo/MG/eS1zJSltQWmiF52KhJ4rVdnYPZR+Iir1RQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/23294.Suzanne_Enoch">About Suzanne Enoch</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/23294.Suzanne_Enoch"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1598379164p3/23294.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/23294.Suzanne_Enoch">Suzanne Enoch
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,088
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16708665390333411729">Suzanne was born in Southern California sometime in the latter half of the 20th century. In the way that some people are born knowing they want to be astronauts or cellists, Suzanne always knew she wanted to be a writer. Early dreams of becoming a zoologist and writing true stories about her adventures in Africa were crushed, however, after she viewed a television special about the world’s most po</span>
  <span id="freeText16708665390333411729" style="display:none">Suzanne was born in Southern California sometime in the latter half of the 20th century. In the way that some people are born knowing they want to be astronauts or cellists, Suzanne always knew she wanted to be a writer. Early dreams of becoming a zoologist and writing true stories about her adventures in Africa were crushed, however, after she viewed a television special about the world’s most poisonous snakes; she did NOT want to write about how she’d been bitten and lost a limb to a cobra. Thankfully at the same time the movie “Star Wars” premiered, and she realized that she could make up adventures and write about them, and not be eaten by deadly predators while doing research.<br /><br />She dabbled in romantic fantasy writing for a year or two after graduating with a degree in English from the University of California, Irvine, until her affection for traditional Regency romances led her to write one for fun. After several encouraging rejections from publishers, she snared the interest of the world’s best and most patient literary agent, who advised her to revise the manuscript. This ultimately led to the publication of her first book, The Black Duke’s Prize, from Avon Books in the Spring of 1995. A second Regency, Angel’s Devil, followed that Fall.<br /><br />When Avon folded its traditional Regency line, Suzanne was encouraged to try her hand at historical romance. As she remained keenly interested in England’s Regency period, she decided to attempt another manuscript set in that time. Lady Rogue hit the shelves in March of 1997. She wrote a total of 29 books for Avon, including two anthologies and a five-part contemporary series which received a pair of starred reviews from Publishers Weekly. One of those books, Twice the Temptation, was named one of the five best romances of the year by PW in 2007.<br /><br />In 2002 her well-known love of all things “Star Wars” led to an invitation to appear on the E! channel in the television special “Star Wars: The Force Is Back”, where she discussed the romance in the movie series and ended up with more air time than George Lucas.<br /><br />In 2010 Suzanne left Avon Books for St. Martin’s Press, where she continues to pen historical romance novels. Her 31st book, Taming an Impossible Rogue, is set to arrive in March 2012.<br /><br />Suzanne is known for her humorous characters, sexy bad boys, and whip-sharp, witty dialogue. She currently resides in Placentia, California with several hundred guppies and various other tropical fish, and handful of very loud, spinach-loving finches. And her collection of action figures and statues from “Star Wars”, “Lord of the Rings”, “X-Men”, and “Pirates of the Caribbean”. Everybody needs some inspiration, after all.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/SuzanneEnoch">www.facebook.com/SuzanneEnoch</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16708665390333411729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
